  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fb2648df-6b28-4143-adb7-293d23e36045'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

<div id="review_180422411" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180422411" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5077124-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326849368p2/5077124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/180422411?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/5077124-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5077124-kathryn?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180422411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6052146115953240541">I have never read this book. Ever. In my life.<br/><br/>But that doesn't matter. I've watched the anime. And my friend has read it and said that they were, like, exactly the same.<br/><br/>So, after saying that, I may get on to my review. *Takes a deep breath."<br/><br/>OMGOMGOMGOMG THIS IS THE BEST SERIES ON THE FUCKING PLANET IT IS HEARTWARMING AND DARK AND ROMANTIC AND FULL OF ACTION AND ABSOLUTELY BEAUTIFUL!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!<br/><br/>Okay, got that out of my system.<br/><br/>This entire series is amazing. I laughed, cried, and bit my nails </span>
  <span id="freeText6052146115953240541" style="display:none">I have never read this book. Ever. In my life.<br /><br />But that doesn't matter. I've watched the anime. And my friend has read it and said that they were, like, exactly the same.<br /><br />So, after saying that, I may get on to my review. *Takes a deep breath."<br /><br />OMGOMGOMGOMG THIS IS THE BEST SERIES ON THE FUCKING PLANET IT IS HEARTWARMING AND DARK AND ROMANTIC AND FULL OF ACTION AND ABSOLUTELY BEAUTIFUL!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!<br /><br />Okay, got that out of my system.<br /><br />This entire series is amazing. I laughed, cried, and bit my nails along with the characters. They are all so diverse and deep and complicated that I swear it's almost like Rumiko wrote about real people. The cast is so large and yet every one of the characters has their own unique look and personality, and that's, like, impossible to do.<br /><br />I am obssessed with this series, and proud of it. I have it as a skin on my laptop. I've written fanfictions about it. I am absolutely in love with the demon Bankotsu (you'll meet him late in the series). I have the freaking TV season box sets. I am the biggest Inuyasha otaku there is. And unashamed to admit it. This series made me sob bitter tears and laugh until my sides hurt. It made me squeal during the romantic moments and scream when something bad happened to a character. I yelled at the TV for twenty minutes when Inuyasha was being an idiot because he almost seems like a real guy (minus the dog ears) making real mistakes. <br /><br />If there is one person on this planet who does not read/watch this series, then God will have failed. Seriously. How any simple human can create comething so otherworldly out of mere pen and paper is amazing. If you are hesitating about buying this... GROW SOME BALLS AND GET IT! YOU WILL NOT BE DISAPPOINTED!!!!!!</span>

<div id="review_528436505" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/528436505" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17215023-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593997066p2/17215023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/528436505?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/17215023-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">any manga reader</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Natalie by: </span>
      friends from middle school 
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=rereading">rereading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=colorful-characters">colorful-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=forest-setting">forest-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=otaku-manga-reading-challenge">otaku-manga-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=shounen-manga">shounen-manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=manga-year-challenge">manga-year-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer528436505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1897210284866840917">Before I go into any detail about this manga let me first go onto a short rant. So I was originally going to do a review on a whole manga series and the same review would be on every volume. But certain manga series (like this one) are over 20 volumes. So I decided to it the series piece by piece and for this review I'm going to go over the first volume and then volumes 2 & 3 will be roughly the same. <br/><br/>So let's get started. <br/><br/>Before I talk about the plot I'm going to talk about my past concerning m</span>
  <span id="freeText1897210284866840917" style="display:none">Before I go into any detail about this manga let me first go onto a short rant. So I was originally going to do a review on a whole manga series and the same review would be on every volume. But certain manga series (like this one) are over 20 volumes. So I decided to it the series piece by piece and for this review I'm going to go over the first volume and then volumes 2 &amp; 3 will be roughly the same. <br /><br />So let's get started. <br /><br />Before I talk about the plot I'm going to talk about my past concerning manga. Aside from <i>Dragon Knights</i> this was the first manga I was introduced to before I became a member of the anime/manga fan community. Since this was the first manga I read, I definitely have a soft spot for it and I absolutely love it despite its flaws. Yes, this manga is not perfect and there are some parts that are completely stupid but I'm to say that those flaws can be found in other manga as well and not just this one. <br /><br />Now let's take a look at the story. <br /><br />So the story is about an ordinary <i>junior high school</i> student who just turned 15 and gets dragged into this medieval world where she is the reincarnation of a priestess who was once the guardian of the powerful jewel called the Shikon Jewel. Her traveling into this fantasy world awakens a sealed half-demon named Inuyasha who was sealed to a tree by a sacred arrow by the deceased priestess Kikyou. A centipede demon chases Kagome and pulls out a powerful jewel out of her body which turns out to be the Shikon jewel. Men and demons come after it and Kagome ends up accidentally shattering the jewel into pieces and scattering them across the land. So now Inuyasha and Kagome have to work together to find pieces of the sacred jewel before anyone else gathers the pieces and becomes stronger with the jewels power.<br /><br />Already in the first volume, this manga sucks you in and here you go for an adventure. The art in the manga is a cutesy art form and the adventure that comes off that pages is really a lot of fun without having to be too complex. So far, the characters are really enjoyable. <br /><br />Kagome is your average fifteen year old girl who’s really fun to follow. I really like how she’s not really annoying given her circumstance. She’s in an unfamiliar place and because of that she can’t help but be in danger. It also doesn’t help that she has the Shikon jewel in her body which attracts demons. She’s nice but also tends to blow in people’s faces if she’s pushed to her limits. <br /><br />Inuyasha is an awesome anti-hero. He doesn’t want to help Kagome gather the jewel shards because it’s the right thing to do. He wants to use the jewel to become a full-fledged demon and get stronger. He’s a typical tough guy who has a soft spot in there somewhere. These two characters are fun to read about and the tension and fights between them is just hilarious. <br /><br />The villain (as of now) is really creative and also fun. Sure, you had human bandits and other demons that tried to get the jewel but those were taken down quickly and their purpose was to take the jewel out of Kagome’s body and to have her break it so the journey can begin. Yura of the hair has an interesting use of hair and actually makes a very dangerous weapon, given that the hair is also invisible as well except for individuals with spiritual powers it makes the hair even that much deadlier. <br /><br />So for a first volume, it’s actually pretty great and brings you in for a big adventure. And by big I mean <b>long</b>. <br /><br /><br />Seriously, this manga is way too long. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1897210284866840917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer1736657636196077169">Why did I ever stop following InuYasha? For a long time, I was reading each volume as it came out. Maybe I got lazy, or maybe I forgot to watch for it. Reading the first volume again reminded me of how much I loved reading it in the first place. It is huge, and it's going to take awhile to get through all of the volumes. (But hey, at least there's a light at the end of this tunnel...) But after reading the first volume, I think it'll be worth it. I really like Rumiko Takahashi's signature style,</span>
  <span id="freeText1736657636196077169" style="display:none">Why did I ever stop following InuYasha? For a long time, I was reading each volume as it came out. Maybe I got lazy, or maybe I forgot to watch for it. Reading the first volume again reminded me of how much I loved reading it in the first place. It is huge, and it's going to take awhile to get through all of the volumes. (But hey, at least there's a light at the end of this tunnel...) But after reading the first volume, I think it'll be worth it. I really like Rumiko Takahashi's signature style, and I love the characters. This was one of my favorite mangas when I first read it, and it still is.</span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Taschenbuch 9783898855235" href="/book/show/6249667-inu-yasha-band-1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=book-to-screen">book-to-screen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=bye-bye-comfort-zone-hello-change">bye-bye-comfort-zone-hello-change</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=cliffhanger">cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=everyone-loved-it-but-me">everyone-loved-it-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=fantasy-or-paranormal">fantasy-or-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=my-summer-2013-company">my-summer-2013-company</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer704302307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10479955094559463694">Giving this manga one star seems harsh but it's pretty much the only rating I feel is right when I think about my "enjoyment" of this first in a series everyone else but me seems to love. To be fair, though, it's more like 1 ½ star.<br/><br/>Anyway, everyone who followed my Black Butler adventure a little (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/576878843' rel='nofollow noopener'>tres</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/577013012' rel='nofollow noopener'>cuatro</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/577753913' rel='nofollow noopener'>cinco</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/606211902' rel='nofollow noopener'>seis</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/623566220' rel='nofollow noopener'>siete</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/623573408' rel='nofollow noopener'>ocho</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648258629' rel='nofollow noopener'>nueve</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/653438177' rel='nofollow noopener'>diez</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/660292199' rel='nofollow noopener'>once</a> is what I'm talking about) might be a witness that it's hard for me to find a manga series where my enjoyment of it is not a constant rollercoas</span>
  <span id="freeText10479955094559463694" style="display:none">Giving this manga one star seems harsh but it's pretty much the only rating I feel is right when I think about my "enjoyment" of this first in a series everyone else but me seems to love. To be fair, though, it's more like 1 ½ star.<br /><br />Anyway, everyone who followed my Black Butler adventure a little (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/576878843" rel="nofollow noopener">tres</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/577013012" rel="nofollow noopener">cuatro</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/577753913" rel="nofollow noopener">cinco</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/606211902" rel="nofollow noopener">seis</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/623566220" rel="nofollow noopener">siete</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/623573408" rel="nofollow noopener">ocho</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648258629" rel="nofollow noopener">nueve</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/653438177" rel="nofollow noopener">diez</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/660292199" rel="nofollow noopener">once</a> is what I'm talking about) might be a witness that it's hard for me to find a manga series where my enjoyment of it is not a constant rollercoaster ride. I love Detective Conan, I love Ouran High School Host Club (though here I've only watched the anime and not read the manga as well) and the other few mangas I've read here and there were sometimes meh (like some of the Black Butler volumes), awesome (like some of the Black Butler volumes), putting me to sleep in a bookstore (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/653438177" rel="nofollow noopener">LIKE SOME OF THE BLACK BUTLER VOLUMES</a>). So my goal is and always will be to find another manga series that I love and adore as much as Detective Conan. And when I saw the first few volumes of Inu Yasha at my library, I picked them up with high hopes.<br /><br />Inu Yasha 01 isn't bad by any means, it's just one of those firsts in a book/manga series that didn't make me feel interested in how the story will continue. Once the manga started, everything happened at once and I was like, wait, can we please slow down a little here? It gave no depth to anything that was happening because there was just too much happening to focus on one thing at a time. This girl literally accidentally time travels and she thinks once or twice about how much she wants to go home and that's it. I know it's a manga and that I shouldn't be expecting too much emotional depth but I WOULD BE FREAKING OUT. Especially considering what shit goes down in the world of Inu Yasha.<br /><br />That's pretty much my only complaint, the missing depth that's too-much-is-happening-at-once's fault. I have the next 5 volumes here, so I'll definitely continue this series and hope that it gets better for me. If that doesn't happen with the next 5 volumes, I won't read any further because ain't nobody got time for a 60 volumes long manga series that you don't enjoy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10479955094559463694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_108354898" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108354898" />
    <a title="Jessica-Robyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3235169-jessica-robyn"><img alt="Jessica-Robyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581748596p2/3235169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108354898?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica-Robyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica-Robyn" href="/user/show/3235169-jessica-robyn">Jessica-Robyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3235169-jessica-robyn?shelf=manga-manhwa">manga-manhwa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3235169-jessica-robyn?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108354898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7486111784602617326">InuYasha is a series that I adore. While I watched the anime I feel in love with the characters and would end up sneaking out of my bedroom late at night to catch the show week after week. It was the show that introduced me to anime and at the time I didn't even know what manga <i>was</i>.<br/><br/>It would make sense for my adoration to transfer itself over to the manga. I mean, they did end the anime series early and it's one of my favourite properties of all time. However, my love for the story and characters</span>
  <span id="freeText7486111784602617326" style="display:none">InuYasha is a series that I adore. While I watched the anime I feel in love with the characters and would end up sneaking out of my bedroom late at night to catch the show week after week. It was the show that introduced me to anime and at the time I didn't even know what manga <i>was</i>.<br /><br />It would make sense for my adoration to transfer itself over to the manga. I mean, they did end the anime series early and it's one of my favourite properties of all time. However, my love for the story and characters may be the one thing that's holding me back really loving the manga. <br /><br />I wasn't incredibly impressed by the first couple of volumes when I read them early last year. The story felt less fluid and the art is in that older style of drawing that I'm not incredibly fond of. It's a difficult adjustment to make, seeing something you love in a different medium and I stopped reading before I was able to adjust to it. <br /><br />Something that's also giving me some difficulty is the story itself. Because the anime was so incredibly faithful to the manga's material (at least as far as I've read), this isn't anything new to me. Even the dialogue matches up word for word in some places. For someone is still cooing over the anime it's hard to really get into the series because that element of surprise, being introduced to something new, not knowing a characters history, motivation, and future, just isn't there any more. <br /><br />So I've marked this series as dropped, but just for now! At some point I am going to read this series then entire way through, all 56 volumes of it, because it is so close to my heart. But it has to be at a point where returning to this doesn't activate my sense of deja vu. <br /><br />If you love something, sometimes you've got to let it go and hope it comes back to you. <br /><br />Now, if you'll excuse me, I have to retreat to my dark corner and cry. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7486111784602617326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_32900232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/32900232" />
    <a title="Chai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1384964-chai"><img alt="Chai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217536292p2/1384964.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/32900232?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chai" href="/user/show/1384964-chai">Chai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32900232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10808144008755368831">I love this series! Rumiko Takahashi returns with a story that has all the comedy of her popular series "Ranma 1/2", but with more attention to plot and character development.<br/><br/>Kagome is a young Japanese highschooler in modern Japan. When she falls in an ancient well on her home property, she finds herself transferred to ancient Japan! There, she discovers she is a reincarnation of a priestess whose job was to protect a magical item called the Shikon Jewel. Ancient Japan is littered with a cast of</span>
  <span id="freeText10808144008755368831" style="display:none">I love this series! Rumiko Takahashi returns with a story that has all the comedy of her popular series "Ranma 1/2", but with more attention to plot and character development.<br /><br />Kagome is a young Japanese highschooler in modern Japan. When she falls in an ancient well on her home property, she finds herself transferred to ancient Japan! There, she discovers she is a reincarnation of a priestess whose job was to protect a magical item called the Shikon Jewel. Ancient Japan is littered with a cast of characters, from talking animals to demons and half-demons. This jewel if in posession of a demon or a half-demon, can make that demon extra powerful and lethal. When Kagome causes the Shikon jewel to shatter, she is forced to pair up with Inuyasha, an unruly half-demon, in order to repair the damage she has done!<br /><br />This series is progressive in a way that Takahashi's "Ranma 1/2" fails to be. Whereas Ranma 1/2 was filled with comedic scenes and the characters' relationships suffered as a result, here Takahashi balances everything out - the plot moves, and at such a thrilling pace! The characters develop, learn, and fall in love, and the comedy is enough to split your sides without subtracting from the overall story's movement.<br /><br />I would recommend this series to any graphic-novel fan. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10808144008755368831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I loved the juxtaposition of the past world of demons with Kagome's modern world. There were parts hat were so sad they brought me close to tears, and parts where I actually chuckled to myself. A true gem in the manga genre, I'd highly recommend it to anyone who loves a good PNR or a great story in general.</span>

<div id="review_540582110" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/540582110" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17619507-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361294823p2/17619507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/540582110?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/17619507-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9784091252012" href="/book/show/22817._1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17619507-sam?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17619507-sam?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17619507-sam?shelf=%E6%97%A5%E6%9C%AC%E8%AA%9E">日本語</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer540582110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13623565757921230388">Another manga book I've read probably a hundred times, haha. Least in English, this is my first in Japanese. Coming off of Detective Conan, I was thinking of trying something a bit different. For Japanese learners, I'll discuss that below.<br/><br/>As for the book content itself:<br/>What can I say? I'm nostalgic. Rereading this again, after so many years, I can hear their voices perfectly, the music thumping in the background, all the sound effects, it was an awesome time to go through this again! I might be </span>
  <span id="freeText13623565757921230388" style="display:none">Another manga book I've read probably a hundred times, haha. Least in English, this is my first in Japanese. Coming off of Detective Conan, I was thinking of trying something a bit different. For Japanese learners, I'll discuss that below.<br /><br />As for the book content itself:<br />What can I say? I'm nostalgic. Rereading this again, after so many years, I can hear their voices perfectly, the music thumping in the background, all the sound effects, it was an awesome time to go through this again! I might be a bit biased, since this series, both as a manga and anime, made up a large part of my childhood. It's a fun adventure series with colorful characters and memorable moments. Lots of fantasy, suspense, mystery, drama, romance, humor, horror, and pretty much every other genre you can think of all rolled up into one.<br /><br />It isn't all perfect though, of course. I have my nit-picks, but given my nostalgia for it, I'm more able to let those things slide. I'm glad the series was able to come to a conclusion, and we got the answers we wanted, and some we didn't even know we wanted. Be warned though, there is a LARGE amount of filler!<br /><br />For the Japanese bit:<br />I was hoping to go into this with an easier time than Detective Conan, since there are much less words per page. Conan is great for beginners sure, but it still took me some time to get through, and I thought I'd feel more successful progress going through a book with significantly less text. To my surprise, it didn't go as planned!<br /><br />The grammar is for sure at least N4, with a few N3/N2 thrown in, but it wasn't just the basics that was throwing me off, it was the archaic vocabulary and super informal speech! So while Conan took me longer, I understood more. Inuyasha went faster, but I understood less. Several old terms, which to be fair, I should've seen coming, and the crudeness with which people speak, also should've seen coming, slowed me down quite a bit. Luckily I found fan translations online (much more true to the original Japanese than officially published translations) and was able to check my work. And for those who don't know, this book DOES include furigana for all kanji, which does help a lot if you're unfamiliar with them!<br /><br />If you're looking to study and trying to find a good first book, DO NOT PICK THIS ONE. Most places that teach you Japanese will NOT prepare you for this. I would recommend Yotsuba (from what I've heard from others) or Detective Conan (from personal experience). If you have a stronger ability of the language, you'll be able to pick up on how to read the informalities, dialects, and colloqualisms of this book, but until then, I'd hold off. Having to look up too many things in a row could hinder motivation. But hey, if you're really that determined, don't let me stop you. Just be ready for having to do some research!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13623565757921230388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_258368740" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258368740" />
    <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions"><img alt="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464118116p2/2602702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258368740?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=manga-manhwa">manga-manhwa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=series-not-finishing">series-not-finishing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258368740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1805648375717438741">This took approximately forever to get through. There are so many freaking volumes. At first, I enjoyed it, because it was kind of funny and silly. Unfortunately, it's incredibly formulaic and repetitive, kind of like episodes of The Power Rangers. You know what's going to happen, but it takes all of time to get there.<br/><br/>Basically, for about fifty of the volumes, they keep having skirmishes with the big bad of the series, Naraku. He's a hanyou like Inuyasha, determined to use the Shikon no Tama to </span>
  <span id="freeText1805648375717438741" style="display:none">This took approximately forever to get through. There are so many freaking volumes. At first, I enjoyed it, because it was kind of funny and silly. Unfortunately, it's incredibly formulaic and repetitive, kind of like episodes of The Power Rangers. You know what's going to happen, but it takes all of time to get there.<br /><br />Basically, for about fifty of the volumes, they keep having skirmishes with the big bad of the series, Naraku. He's a hanyou like Inuyasha, determined to use the Shikon no Tama to become a full youkai and to be the most powerful dude in the world. He creates an evil league of evil to help him in his quest, and is generally a pain. Worst of all, whenever the good guys are winning a battle, he dematerializes, so that he can fight another day. Can anyone explain to me why only the bad guys have this power?<br /><br />Speaking of power, Inuyasha and his brother have a lot of it, more than anyone else apparently. Apparently being hanyou is to power as being a muggle-born witch has to do with magical ability, which is to say that it has very little to do with it. However, what drove me completely crazy was that Inuyasha has like three attacks for thirty-some volumes of the series. He doesn't learn anything! He continues to fight like an idiot, and finally gets attacks because other people help him out. Inuyasha does not really seem like a hero who would be able to defeat anyone intelligent enough to target his weaknesses.<br /><br />Okay, so as a shounen, it's not that great, because the action is so mindless and repetitive. How about the romance elements? Those are better at least, right? Not in my opinion. For longer than I deem acceptable, Inuyasha continues to be torn between Kagome and Kikyou. I get that it's a complicated situation, but that is so not cool. Plus, Kagome's like 14 or something at the beginning. Sheesh.<br /><br />The other romance of the series is Houshi and Sango, which I definitely did not ship either. Houshi really creeps me out because of the way he asks every woman he meets if she'll bear his child. Sango would probably be my favorite character, because she kicks so much ass, but she always becomes so girly and not like herself around Houshi. Ugh!<br /><br />The art is not great, though it does have a certain charm. However, this charm dissipates over time. In a lot of long manga series, the art gets better along the way, but not so here.<br /><br />This definitely turned out not to be my thing. The story is weak (seriously, how did Kagome pass middle school?) and so is the characterization. However, this is one of the most popular manga there is, so keep in mind that lots of people probably would not agree with my reactions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1805648375717438741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sevairi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8809208-sevairi"><img alt="Sevairi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548906730p2/8809208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1091360263?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sevairi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sevairi" href="/user/show/8809208-sevairi">Sevairi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1091360263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18431572377280930542"><b>EDIT:</b> I found awesome scans of this manga on my tablet's manga reader which is translated directly from the Japanese. I've edited this review after reading these. My original review was based off an altered reprint copy.<br/><br/><br/><br/>Okay, so once again, this review comes after rereading the first volume. <br/><br/>I've always had a warm spot in my heart for InuYasha. It was the first anime I ever watched, which I stumbled upon by flicking through television channels at ten o'clock on a Saturday night. It was the first</span>
  <span id="freeText18431572377280930542" style="display:none"><b>EDIT:</b> I found awesome scans of this manga on my tablet's manga reader which is translated directly from the Japanese. I've edited this review after reading these. My original review was based off an altered reprint copy.<br /><br /><br /><br />Okay, so once again, this review comes after rereading the first volume. <br /><br />I've always had a warm spot in my heart for InuYasha. It was the first anime I ever watched, which I stumbled upon by flicking through television channels at ten o'clock on a Saturday night. It was the first manga I ever purchased and read. It's the reason why I draw in an anime style.<br /><br />I love Rumiko Takahashi's drawing style. I love it. Love love love it. The artwork within the pages is wonderful, ESPECIALLY the coloured pages. Oh my god, the coloured pages. Not to mentioned the coloured prints at the end of the volume. Kikyo looks so much more badass in the manga. And Mistress Centipede looks way more gruesome after swallowing the Shikon no Tama. <br /><br />Takahashi has a good way of telling a story in this first volume, as well. Not just the artwork, but the actual writing. This volume begins in the Sengoku Jidai, or the Warring States, era of Japan, where Takahashi sets up one of the main plotlines of the series. The old history nerd in me can't get enough of it.<br /><br />Now, I've read the first few volumes of InuYasha several times. I've read it translated straight from the Japanese, as well as altered English copies. Personally, I prefer the manga as translated straight from Japanese better. I like that it still keeps a lot of the Japanese terms, and I feel like the story telling just flows better. <br /><br />Moving on, I'm pretty sure Yura of the Hair is my favourite female villain in this series. I don't even know why. She's girlish and fierce and all kinds of wildly sexy. I don't really understand why she says "la" all the time, but I'm willing to overlook it. I really wish we could see more of her in this series than what we do.<br /><br />I really don't think I have anything bad to say. Takahashi doesn't waste time diving into the plot, and sets up the plot line nicely in the first volume. The artwork is adorable and she has a wide range of interesting characters (Kagome's grandfather kills me). The pacing is perfect, too.<br /><br />I'm so glad I reread this. I forgot how much I loved this series.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_262763350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/262763350" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4634710-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303178484p2/4634710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/262763350?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/4634710-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781421519784" href="/book/show/2291509.Inuyasha_Vol_1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4634710-rebecca?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262763350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16786780030483676501">InuYasha is my very first manga and I had a lot of fun reading it. I am very glad I never saw the cartoon series, so that I was reading InuYasha with fresh eyes. I really appreciated the note at the beginning of the story explaining why InuYasha is set Between 1482-1558 They said:<br/><br/>“ because it was relatively easier to draw out a ghost story from that time period…in the Sengoku Era, there was war, and lots of people died.”<br/><br/>I had never thought about all the research that would go into a graphic nove</span>
  <span id="freeText16786780030483676501" style="display:none">InuYasha is my very first manga and I had a lot of fun reading it. I am very glad I never saw the cartoon series, so that I was reading InuYasha with fresh eyes. I really appreciated the note at the beginning of the story explaining why InuYasha is set Between 1482-1558 They said:<br /><br />“ because it was relatively easier to draw out a ghost story from that time period…in the Sengoku Era, there was war, and lots of people died.”<br /><br />I had never thought about all the research that would go into a graphic novel or manga before, yes I know stupid on my part, but the note at the beginning really set up the story for me.<br /> <br />Kagome doesn’t care about all the stories her grandfather tells her, she is your normal self absorbed teenage girl. When she gets sucked into the past/other world, all this has to change. I liked Kagome. She reminded me of Sailor Moon ( but less winey). Kagome had a lot to deal with: Crazy demon things coming at her every time she turned around, an old woman trying to tell her what to do, a hot half demon that she can’t decide to trust or not, and some cool new powers. When it was between Kagome running from a fight or helping people, she would help and that is what made me like her.<br /><br />InuYasha is the half demon that has been trapped/dead until Kagome came into his world. Kagome looks exactly like Kikyo, the one that trapped him. All InuYasha says he wants is the Jewel of Four Souls to make himself all demon. Well for someone who just wants a jewel he sure does save Kagome, and not the jewel on occasion. And there is definitely some attraction and tension going both ways for these two.<br /><br />There were some really funny moments too. Kagome discovered she had power over InuYasha and would look at him say the words “Sit Boy” and his body would immediately do it! Um…I want that power with a few people. Is that bad? Anyway I can’t wait to read more in this series. It’s so much fun!<br /><br />Happy Reading,<br />Rebecca<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bendingthespine.blogspot.com">www.bendingthespine.blogspot.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16786780030483676501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55943309?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/1350602-laura">Laura</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55943309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13768193565883573347">I got hooked on the InuYasha series back when it was available to be viewed at a reasonable time of day on the Cartoon Network. When I moved to a new home and discovered that our community cable service was running InuYasha at 5:30am my addiction to this series went on hiatus. I wanted to know if the series had an end and if so how Ms. Takahasi decided to conclude this story. Happily I found the entire manga series had been scanned, in English, all 558 volumes. I finally was able to find out wha</span>
  <span id="freeText13768193565883573347" style="display:none">I got hooked on the InuYasha series back when it was available to be viewed at a reasonable time of day on the Cartoon Network. When I moved to a new home and discovered that our community cable service was running InuYasha at 5:30am my addiction to this series went on hiatus. I wanted to know if the series had an end and if so how Ms. Takahasi decided to conclude this story. Happily I found the entire manga series had been scanned, in English, all 558 volumes. I finally was able to find out what happened to InuYasha, Kagome, Sango, Mirouku, Shippo, Kahuko and Kikiyo and of course, Naraku. The characters matured and were each able to find their own unique strengths and powers. I have to say I am glad I don't speak or read Japanese. It appears InuYasha was given something of a potty mouth, at least by my standards. It was nice to see how his character manages to mellow out some by the end of the series. The story ends in a very satisfying way for me, at least. For those unfamiliar with this story line, a brief summation: Kagome, a modern day, junior high age, teenager falls down a well on family property and finds herself transported back in time to Feudal Age Japan and in addition finds out that she is the reincarnation both, physically and spiritually, of a priestess endowed with power to fight evil forces running rampant in the country at that time. Upon her arrival she immediately encounters InuYasha who is half demon and half human and has been sealed by an arrow to a tree for 50 years. How an why these two beings meet and how they join forces is the meat of this series. It is available for viewing and your reading pleasure at onemanga.com</span>
  <a data-text-id="13768193565883573347" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5255217-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574126098p2/5255217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1136015291?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/5255217-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5255217-julie?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1136015291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11208949837588962821">the shameless manga reviewing continues with another manga that dominated my teen life, INUYASHA.<br/><br/>I remember seeing the anime on Adult Swim before tracking down the comic. back then when Adult Swim was still pretty fresh, I would TAPE (yes, TAPE) the anime hours and one night I happened to have an episode of Inuyasha on my tape. then the madness started.<br/><br/>Inuyasha is a story set in early medieval Japan which is what I think makes it so interesting. the focus is on what happens on the other side of </span>
  <span id="freeText11208949837588962821" style="display:none">the shameless manga reviewing continues with another manga that dominated my teen life, INUYASHA.<br /><br />I remember seeing the anime on Adult Swim before tracking down the comic. back then when Adult Swim was still pretty fresh, I would TAPE (yes, TAPE) the anime hours and one night I happened to have an episode of Inuyasha on my tape. then the madness started.<br /><br />Inuyasha is a story set in early medieval Japan which is what I think makes it so interesting. the focus is on what happens on the other side of Kagome's well, less on what happens in her world (modern day Japan). the series (both anime and manga) are not very superfluous either which I find refreshing compared to other anime/manga that are just too flashy. here we have normal hair colors, accurate historical clothing, a nice balance of humor, drama and action, etc. I remember laughing and crying as well as sitting on the edge of my seat while plowing through this series.<br /><br />the only problem with Inuyasha is WHY THE FUCK IS IT SO LONG?! I mean it's a good story but come on! at nearly 50 volumes of graphic novels (all about 250 pages each), one definitely starts to feel the fatigue. yet, this is Rumiko Takahashi's trademark. note that Ranma 1/2 was very lengthy as well, but only to about 38 volumes. Takahashi has a tendency to take an idea and then just repeat that theme in various abstractions throughout her series which is what causes some of her works to be so stinkin' long. <br /><br />this "technique" of Takahashi works can get very annoying, but with Inuyasha, it is worth the wait and annoyance.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11208949837588962821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11837594164715332198" style="display:none">This manga starts off with a prologue that if you haven't at least seen the show and gotten the legend of InuYasha then shame on you. <br />Well a young half dog demon, InuYasha, steals a spiritual jewel named the Shikon no Tama. Suddenly he is shot, by the head priestess Kikyo, with a sealing arrow. While dying she makes her younger sister burn the jewel with her on her funeral pyre. From then on the jewel had never been seen again.<br />There the story stands.<br />All of a sudden we are thrown into modern day society. There still stands a shrine in Tokyo. We find a normal run of the mill family. A mother, her two children, and their grandfather. Never stated in the entire manga anything about a father, but it may have been something that escaped my notice when I read this so long ago. <br />It happens to be Kagome's fifteenth birthday, and she has to retrieve her cat Buyo from the dried up well house.<br />Suddenly a cinnapide demon drags her across the ages litterally. How is this possible you'll have to read the manga for yourself to find out!<br />Come and join in on one of my favorite series of all time.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12150829735392386504">i was addicted to this show. addicted! it was to the point where i had downloaded and viewed up to episode 167. (that means i d/led over 140 episodes over the couple year span that i had to watch it.) i must admit, i wouldn't have given the show the time of day if it weren't for that awesome ending credits theme song. yes, you know the one, "my way." that song alone was addictive. there were other addictive songs too, but that one remained my favorite. but i think i'm suppose to be talking about</span>
  <span id="freeText12150829735392386504" style="display:none">i was addicted to this show. addicted! it was to the point where i had downloaded and viewed up to episode 167. (that means i d/led over 140 episodes over the couple year span that i had to watch it.) i must admit, i wouldn't have given the show the time of day if it weren't for that awesome ending credits theme song. yes, you know the one, "my way." that song alone was addictive. there were other addictive songs too, but that one remained my favorite. but i think i'm suppose to be talking about the book, and not the show here.<br /><br />the book is just as good as the series. i had always felt that it was slow to start. regardless of that actually being true or not. takahashi does get straight to the point about needing to collect the shards, so i think i'm being more than slightly unfair. it's neat seeing takahashi's style come through, it's smoothed over in the show. i love inuyasha and kagome's interactions. i'm hoping that as the series progresses, it starts to deviate from the tv show a bit, in a better way. if it doesn't i might have to give up on this series, like i had to for the show. </span>

<div id="review_2072462549" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2072462549" />
    <a title="Cupcakes &amp; Machetes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23809381-cupcakes-machetes"><img alt="Cupcakes &amp; Machetes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585747298p2/23809381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

  <span id="freeText2407893995468789846" style="display:none">It’s been years since I binged watched the entire Inu-yasha anime, so I thought, why not give the manga a try? My next question is; if you read it from front to back like a normal book is it really a manga? I’ve not read many but the ones I have you read from back to front.<br><br>Either way, from what I can remember the show must stick to the books fairly well. Reading this just makes me want to watch the show all over again. But, I guess instead I could continue with the books. Even if the books insist on showing me 15 year old boobies.<br><br>Despite that, it’s a fun origin story. If you’ve never heard of it, but enjoy things involving demons, magical shards, sass, and heros, give this a try.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501074233i/23414451.jpg" width="500" height="372" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6969967299264989746">Melissa Wickelhaus<br/>Genre: Modern Fantasy<br/>Volume one of Inu-Yasha: A Feudal Fairy Tale follows Kagome, a typical Japanese high school girl until one day when an evil monster pulls her through the old well in the shrine behind her family’s home. Kagome is pulled from her world into the world of Japan’s ancient past where many of the legends her grandfather has told her about turn out to be true. Kagome may just be the reincarnation of a village priestess and she must work together with the half-demo</span>
  <span id="freeText6969967299264989746" style="display:none">Melissa Wickelhaus<br />Genre: Modern Fantasy<br />Volume one of Inu-Yasha: A Feudal Fairy Tale follows Kagome, a typical Japanese high school girl until one day when an evil monster pulls her through the old well in the shrine behind her family’s home. Kagome is pulled from her world into the world of Japan’s ancient past where many of the legends her grandfather has told her about turn out to be true. Kagome may just be the reincarnation of a village priestess and she must work together with the half-demon Inu-Yasha to retrieve the shards of the Shikon Jewel. The art is clean and clear and the action scenes really draw the reader into the story. Overall this manga is well done, and I highly recommend it.<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HbM0+DOL9d67N49UQ8Is0O73Hxz8/k1u7LhOXHFGvmre/Sqb5TJ7hK0Dj8qF3aORl24M7S0s5v95TqqXBWWBeA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/12948.Rumiko_Takahashi">About Rumiko Takahashi</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/12948.Rumiko_Takahashi"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1599583550p3/12948.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/12948.Rumiko_Takahashi">Rumiko Takahashi
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13233540618418193520">Rumiko Takahashi (高橋 留美子) was born in Niigata, Japan. She is not only one of the richest women in Japan but also one of the top paid manga artists. She is also the most successful female comic artist in history. She has been writing manga non-stop for 31 years.<br/><br/>Rumiko Takahashi is one of the wealthiest women in Japan. The manga she creates (and its anime adaptations) are very popular in the United </span>
  <span id="freeText13233540618418193520" style="display:none">Rumiko Takahashi (高橋 留美子) was born in Niigata, Japan. She is not only one of the richest women in Japan but also one of the top paid manga artists. She is also the most successful female comic artist in history. She has been writing manga non-stop for 31 years.<br /><br />Rumiko Takahashi is one of the wealthiest women in Japan. The manga she creates (and its anime adaptations) are very popular in the United States and Europe where they have been released as both manga and anime in English translation. Her works are relatively famous worldwide, and many of her series were some of the forerunners of early English language manga to be released in the nineties. Takahashi is also the best selling female comics artist in history; well over 100 million copies of her various works have been sold.<br /><br />Though she was said to occasionally doodle in the margins of her papers while attending Niigata Chūō High School, Takahashi's interest in manga did not come until later. During her college years, she enrolled in Gekiga Sonjuku, a manga school founded by Kazuo Koike, mangaka of Crying Freeman and Lone Wolf and Cub. Under his guidance Rumiko Takahashi began to publish her first doujinshi creations in 1975, such as Bye-Bye Road and Star of Futile Dust. Kozue Koike often urged his students to create well-thought out, interesting characters, and this influence would greatly impact Rumiko Takahashi's works throughout her career.<br /><br />Career and major works:<br /><br />Takahashi's professional career began in 1978. Her first published story was Those Selfish Aliens, a comedic science fiction story. During the same year, she published Time Warp Trouble, Shake Your Buddha, and the Golden Gods of Poverty in Shōnen Sunday, which would remain the home to most of her major works for the next twenty years. Later that year, Rumiko attempted her first full-length series, Urusei Yatsura. Though it had a rocky start due to publishing difficulties, Urusei Yatsura would become one of the most beloved anime and manga comedies in Japan.<br /><br />In 1980, Rumiko Takahashi found her niche and began to publish with regularity. At this time she started her second major series, Maison Ikkoku, in Big Comic Spirits. Written for an older audience, Maison Ikkoku is often considered to be one of the all-time best romance manga. Takahashi managed to work on Maison Ikkoku on and off simultaneously with Urusei Yatsura. She concluded both series in 1987, with Urusei Yatsura ending at 34 volumes, and Maison Ikkoku being 15.<br /><br />During the 1980s, Takahashi became a prolific writer of short story manga, which is surprising considering the massive lengths of most of her works. Her stories The Laughing Target, Maris the Chojo, and Fire Tripper all were adapted into original video animations (OVAs). In 1984, after the end of Urusei Yatsura and Maison Ikkoku, Takahashi took a different approach to storytelling and began the dark, macabre Mermaid Saga. This series of short segments was published sporadically until 1994, with the final story being Mermaid's Mask. Many fans contend that this work remains unfinished by Takahashi, since the final story does not end on a conclusive note.<br /><br />Another short work left untouched is One-Pound Gospel, which, like Mermaid Saga, was published erratically. The last story to be drawn was published in 2001, however just recently she wrote one final chapter concluding the series<br /><br />Later in 1987, Takahashi began her third major series, Ranma ½. Following the late 80s and early 90s trend of shōnen martial arts manga, Ranma ½ features a gender-bending twist. The series continued for nearly a decade until 1996, when it ended at 38 volumes. Ranma ½ is one of Rumiko Takahashi's most popular series with the Western world.<br /><br />During the later half of the 1990s, Rumiko Takahashi continued with short stories and her installments of Mermaid Saga and One-Pound Gospel until beginning her fourth major work, InuYasha. While Ran</span>
